UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 AN ACT relating to fiscal matters and declaring an emergency.
2 Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Kentucky:
3 SECTION 1. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 141 IS CREATED TO
4 READ AS FOLLOWS:
5 (1) As used in this section:
6 (a) "Approved company" has the same meaning as in Section 13 of this Act;
7 (b) "Authority" has the same meaning as in Section 13 of this Act; and
8 (c) "Credit" means the economic development credit provided to an approved
9 company by the authority in accordance with Section 17 of this Act.
10 (2) (a) For taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2026, there shall be
11 allowed an economic development credit to an approved company. The
12 credit shall be refundable, nontransferable, and allowed against the tax
13 imposed under KRS 141.020 or 141.040 and 141.0401, with the ordering of
14 the credit as provided in Section 2 of this Act.
15 (b) In the case of a pass-through entity not subject to the tax imposed by KRS
16 141.040, the credit shall be taken against the tax imposed by KRS 141.0401
17 and shall be claimed by the partners, members, or shareholders in
18 accordance with their proportionate share of income.
19 (c) The amount of the credit that may be claimed in a taxable year by the
20 approved company shall be equal to the amount determined in accordance
21 with Section 17 of this Act, as applicable, except the total amount of credits
22 claimed by all approved companies under Section 17 of this Act shall not
23 exceed four million dollars ($4,000,000) per taxable year, of which no more
24 than one million dollars ($1,000,000) shall be allowed for wages paid to
25 full-time employees in counties other than heritage counties.
26 (3) (a) The department shall:
27 1. Promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS
Page 1 of 217
HB086920.100 - 469 - XXXX 4/15/2026 11:03 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 Chapter 13A to administer the credit;
2 2. Work with the authority to determine the approved amount of credit or
3 apportionable share of credit available to be claimed in any taxable
4 year on a return as filed by an approved company or each partner,
5 member, or shareholder of an approved company; and
6 3. Report the following to the authority on the credits claimed under this
7 section:
8 a. The total amount of credit awarded for each taxable year, by
9 county;
10 b. Each taxpayer claiming a credit; and
11 c. The total amount of wages paid to a full-time employee by an
12 approved company and included in its credit computation.
13 (b) The information required to be reported under this subsection shall not be
14 considered confidential taxpayer information and shall not be subject to
15 KRS Chapter 131 or any other provisions of the Kentucky Revised Statutes
16 prohibiting disclosure or reporting of information.

4 Section 3. KRS 131.190 is amended to read as follows:
5 (1) No present or former commissioner or employee of the department, present or
6 former member of a county board of assessment appeals, present or former property
7 valuation administrator or employee, present or former secretary or employee of the
8 Finance and Administration Cabinet, former secretary or employee of the Revenue
9 Cabinet, or any other person, shall intentionally and without authorization inspect
10 or divulge any information acquired by him or her of the affairs of any person, or
11 information regarding the tax schedules, returns, or reports required to be filed with
12 the department or other proper officer, or any information produced by a hearing or
13 investigation, insofar as the information may have to do with the affairs of the
14 person's business.
15 (2) The prohibition established by subsection (1) of this section shall not extend to:
16 (a) Information required in prosecutions for making false reports or returns of
17 property for taxation, or any other infraction of the tax laws;
18 (b) Any matter properly entered upon any assessment record, or in any way made
19 a matter of public record;
20 (c) Furnishing any taxpayer or his or her properly authorized agent with
21 information respecting his or her own return;
22 (d) Testimony provided by the commissioner or any employee of the department
23 in any court, or the introduction as evidence of returns or reports filed with the
24 department, in an action for violation of state or federal tax laws or in any
25 action challenging state or federal tax laws;
26 (e) Providing an owner of unmined coal, oil or gas reserves, and other mineral or
27 energy resources assessed under KRS 132.820, or owners of surface land

11 208;

1 (23)[(22)] (a) "Qualified company" means any corporation, limited liability company,
2 partnership, limited partnership, sole proprietorship, business trust, or any
3 other legal entity through which business is conducted that is engaged in or is
4 planning to be engaged in one (1) or more of the following activities within
5 the Commonwealth:
6 1. Manufacturing;
7 2. Agribusiness;
8 3. Nonretail service or technology;
9 4. Headquarter operations, regardless of the underlying business activity of
10 the company;
11 5. Alternative fuel, gasification, energy-efficient alternative fuel, or
12 renewable energy production;
13 6. Carbon dioxide or hydrogen transmission pipeline;
14 7. Coal severing and processing; or
15 8. Hospital operations.
16 (b) "Qualified company" does not include companies where the primary activity
17 to be conducted within the Commonwealth is forestry, fishing, the provision
18 of utilities, construction, wholesale trade, retail trade, real estate, rental and
19 leasing, accommodation and food services, or public administration services;
20 (24)[(23)] "Renewable energy production" means the same as in KRS 154.32-010;
21 (25)[(24)] "Skills upgrade training" means employee training sponsored by a qualified
22 company that is designed to provide the employee with new skills necessary to
23 enhance productivity, improve performance, or retain employment, including but
24 not limited to technical and interpersonal skills, and training that is designed to
25 enhance computer skills, communication skills, problem solving, reading, writing,
26 or math skills of employees who are unable to function effectively on the job due to
27 deficiencies in these areas, are unable to advance on the job, or who risk

5 imposed by KRS 141.0401, as provided in this subchapter; and
6 (27)[(26)] "Technical assistance" means professional and any other assistance provided
7 by qualified companies to an educational institution, which is reasonably calculated
8 to support directly the development and expansion of a particular program as

10 Section 5. KRS 154.12-207 is amended to read as follows:
11 (1) The corporation may, subject to appropriation from the General Assembly or from
12 funds made available to the corporation from any other public or private source,
13 provide grants-in-aid to qualified companies, not in excess of five hundred thousand
14 dollars ($500,000) per grant-in-aid. Such grants-in-aid shall be used exclusively for
15 programs which are consistent with the provisions of this chapter.
16 (2) The corporation may, in accordance with KRS 154.12-204 to 154.12-208, award a
17 skills training investment credit to an approved company. The amount of the skills
18 training investment credit awarded by the corporation shall be an amount not to
19 exceed fifty percent (50%) of the amount of approved costs incurred by the
20 approved company in connection with its program of occupational upgrade training
21 or skills upgrade training, the credit amount not to exceed four thousand five
22 hundred dollars ($4,500)[two thousand dollars ($2,000)] per trainee for an
23 approved company in a heritage county and three thousand five hundred dollars
24 ($3,500) per trainee for an approved company located in any other county, and, in
25 the aggregate, not to exceed five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000) for each
26 approved company per fiscal year. The corporation shall only approve one (1)
27 application per fiscal year for each approved company.
Page 15 of 217
HB086920.100 - 469 - XXXX 4/15/2026 11:03 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 (3) To apply for a grant-in-aid or a skills training investment credit, a qualified
2 company shall submit an application to the Bluegrass State Skills Corporation
3 before commencing its program of skills upgrade or occupational upgrade training.
4 Each application shall contain information the corporation requires, including but
5 not limited to:
6 (a) A proposal for a program of skills upgrade training, occupational upgrade
7 training, and education;
8 (b) A description of each component of the proposed training program and the
9 number of employee training hours requested; and
10 (c) A statement of the total anticipated costs and expenses of the program,
11 including a breakdown of the costs associated with equipment, personnel,
12 facilities, and materials.
13 (4) Approval of the grant-in-aid and skills training investment credit application by the
14 board shall be based upon the following criteria:
15 (a) The program must be within the scope of KRS 154.12-204 to 154.12-208;
16 (b) Participants in the program must qualify as an employee as defined by KRS
17 154.12-204;
18 (c) The program must involve an area of skills upgrade training, occupational
19 upgrade training, and education which is needed by a qualified company and
20 for which a shortage of qualified individuals exists within the
21 Commonwealth; and
22 (d) The grant-in-aid and skills training investment credit must be essential to the

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 (1) The purposes of this subchapter are:
2 (a) To provide incentives for eligible companies and to encourage the location or
3 expansion of manufacturing facilities, agribusiness operations, nonretail
4 service or technology facilities, headquarters operations, alternative fuel
5 production facilities, gasification production facilities, energy-efficient
6 alternative fuel production facilities, renewable energy production facilities,
7 carbon dioxide or hydrogen transmission pipelines, coal severing and
8 processing, and hospital operations in the Commonwealth to advance the
9 public purposes of:
10 1. Creation of new jobs that, but for the incentives offered by the authority,
11 would not exist within the Commonwealth;
12 2. Creation of new sources of tax revenues for the support of public
13 services provided by the Commonwealth;
14 3. Improvement in the quality of life for Kentucky citizens through the
15 creation of sustainable jobs with higher salaries; and
16 4. Providing an economic stimulus to bolster in-state production of vital
17 medications and personal protective equipment; and
18 (b) To provide balanced[enhanced] incentives for companies that locate in
19 heritage[enhanced incentive] counties in recognition of the depressed
20 economic conditions in those counties and the increased need for the growth
21 and development caused by the depressed economic conditions.
22 (2) To qualify for the incentives provided by subsection (3) of this section, an approved
23 company shall:
24 (a) Incur eligible costs of at least one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000);
25 (b) Create at least ten (10) new full-time jobs and maintain an annual average
26 number of at least ten (10) new full-time jobs; and
27 (c) 1. Pay at least ninety percent (90%) of all new full-time employees whose

9 number of economic development projects.

18 as they are made available within the Commonwealth.

20 and planning that may have an effect on community members, system staff, and
21 students.

17 SECTION 42. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 141 IS CREATED TO
18 READ AS FOLLOWS:
19 (1) As used in this section:
20 (a) "Agriculturally based alternative jet fuel" means an alternative jet fuel
21 produced from agricultural biomass, including crops and agricultural
22 byproducts derived from agricultural or livestock production, such as corn,
23 soybeans, wheat, canola, animal fats, and biomass residues from trees,
24 wood, and grasses;
25 (b) "Alternative jet fuel" means a liquid fuel that can be used in an aircraft
26 without the need to modify the aircraft engines or existing fuel distribution
27 infrastructure, and that:
Page 133 of 217
HB086920.100 - 469 - XXXX 4/15/2026 11:03 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 1. Consists of synthesized hydrocarbons and meets the requirements of:
2 a. The American Society for Testing and Materials International
3 Standard D7566; or
4 b. The American Society for Testing and Materials International
5 Standard D1655;
6 2. Is derived from eligible feedstocks;
7 3. Is not derived from palm fatty acid distillates; and
8 4. Achieves at least a fifty percent (50%) lifecycle greenhouse gas
9 emissions reduction in comparison with petroleum-based jet fuel, as
10 determined by a test that shows the fuel production pathway achieves
11 at least a fifty percent (50%) reduction of the aggregate attributional
12 care lifecycle by measuring either:
13 a. Emissions under the lifecycle methodology for alternative jet
14 fuels adopted by the International Civil Aviation Organization
15 with the agreement of the United States; or
16 b. Greenhouse gas emissions values utilizing the most recent
17 version of Argonne National Laboratory's GREET model;
18 (c) "Alternative jet fuel producer" means an entity in this state that:
19 1. Produces alternative jet fuel; or
20 2. Blends SBC with conventional aviation gasoline or jet fuel;
21 (d) "Eligible feedstock" means any feedstock that qualifies as an eligible
22 feedstock for purposes of Section 45Z of the Internal Revenue Code;
23 (e) "Eligible taxpayer" means an alternative jet fuel producer or feedstock
24 provider that is located in the Commonwealth;
25 (f) "Feedstock provider" means an entity that manufactures an eligible
26 feedstock, including SBC, used in the process of making alternative jet fuel;
27 and
Page 134 of 217
HB086920.100 - 469 - XXXX 4/15/2026 11:03 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 (g) "Synthetic blending component" or "SBC" means synthesized
2 hydrocarbons that meet the requirements in any one (1) of the annexes of
3 the American Society for Testing and Materials International Standard
4 D7566, which may then be used as a component in the manufacture of
5 alternative jet fuel.
6 (2) (a) There shall be allowed a nonrefundable, nontransferable alternative jet fuel
7 credit allowed against the taxes imposed in KRS 141.020 or 141.040 and
8 141.0401 for alternative jet fuel producers in an amount certified by the
9 department under this section, with the ordering of the credits as provided
10 in Section 2 of this Act.
11 (b) For taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2029, but before
12 January 1, 2035, an eligible taxpayer may claim a credit at a rate of:
13 1. Fifty cents ($0.50) per gallon to a feedstock provider supplying either
14 eligible feedstocks or SBC to an alternative jet fuel producer;
15 2. One dollar and fifty cents ($1.50) per gallon to an alternative jet fuel
16 producer that processes eligible feedstocks or blends SBC with
17 conventional jet fuel to produce alternative jet fuel;
18 3. Two dollars ($2) per gallon to an alternative jet fuel producer that
19 processes eligible feedstocks or blends SBC with conventional jet fuel
20 to produce agriculturally based alternative jet fuel; or
21 4. Two dollars and fifty cents ($2.50) per gallon to an alternative jet fuel
22 producer that processes eligible feedstocks or blends SBC with
23 conventional jet fuel to produce an agriculturally based alternative jet
24 fuel using an eligible feedstock that was produced in the
25 Commonwealth.
26 (3) (a) The credit allowed in subsection (2) of this section shall not be carried
27 forward to other taxable years.
Page 135 of 217
HB086920.100 - 469 - XXXX 4/15/2026 11:03 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 (b) The total credit allowed in subsection (2)(b)1. and 2. of this section shall not
2 exceed two million dollars ($2,000,000) per eligible taxpayer per taxable
3 year.
4 (c) The credits allowed in subsection (2) of this section may stack if the
5 alternative jet fuel producer is the same as the feedstock provider and shall
6 not exceed three dollars ($3) per gallon per entity.
7 (d) The aggregate total credit certified in a calendar year shall not exceed
8 twenty million dollars ($20,000,000). If the aggregate total of credits
9 certified exceeds twenty million dollars ($20,000,000), the department shall
10 apportion credits pro rata among eligible taxpayers up to the twenty million
11 dollar ($20,000,000) limit.
12 (4) The department, in conjunction with the Kentucky Department of Agriculture
13 and the Energy and Environment Cabinet, shall promulgate emergency and
14 ordinary administrative regulations in accordance with KRS Chapter 13A to
15 adopt:
16 (a) Forms and procedures necessary for implementation, calculation,
17 reporting, and certification of the credit no later than October 1, 2028;
18 (b) Verification standards and processes to ensure the fuel meets the
19 requirements to be alternative jet fuel or agriculturally based alternative jet
20 fuel; and
21 (c) Verification standards and processes to ensure each alternative jet fuel
22 producer and feedstock provider meets the criteria established in subsection
23 (1)(c) and (f) of this section.
24 (5) The department, Kentucky Department of Agriculture, and Energy and
25 Environment Cabinet shall report to the Interim Joint Committee on
26 Appropriations and Revenue when administrative regulations have been
27 promulgated under subsection (4) of this section, and the credit provided in this
Page 136 of 217

1 section shall not be approved prior to the report.

3 advertisement placement, communication, other act connected
4 with the unlawful conduct; and

6 unlawful by KRS 367.170, even if arising from the same
7 transaction or directed at the same consumer; and
8 2. Any method, act, or practice declared unlawful by KRS 367.170 that is
9 not identified as being in connection with a specific identifiable person
10 or transaction, but that is continuing in nature, shall constitute a
11 separate violation for each day that the unlawful method, act, or
12 practice exists or continues.
13 (c) Proof of actual injury to a consumer as a prerequisite to the assessment of
14 civil penalties under this subsection shall not be required, as the civil
15 penalty provisions in this subsection are intended to punish and deter the
16 violator and not intended solely to compensate injured parties.
17 (d) In determining the amount of the civil penalty established in paragraph (a)
18 of this subsection to be assessed for each violation, the trier of fact may
19 consider, either alone or in combination, the following factors:

22 2. The nature, extent, and severity of the injury to consumers and the
23 public;
24 3. The person's ability to pay;
25 4. The amount of profit or gain obtained through the unlawful conduct;

27 6. The desire to eliminate any benefit derived from the violation and to

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS HB 869/EN
1 deter future violations; and
2 7. Any prior violations of KRS 367.170 by the person.
3 (e) For purposes of this subsection, "person" has the same meaning as in KRS
4 367.110.
5 (f) This subsection shall:
6 1. Be liberally construed to effectuate its purpose of protecting
7 consumers and the public from unfair, false, misleading, or deceptive
8 acts or practices, and to provide the Attorney General the enforcement
9 tools necessary to deter unlawful conduct; and
10 2. Not be construed to limit the:
11 a. Methods by which the Attorney General or trier of fact may
12 determine the number of violations in any particular action; or
13 b. Right of the trier of fact to determine the number of violations
